тАШ рд░рдпрд┐рд░реНрди’ рдЗрддрд┐ рджрд╢рд░реНрдЪрдВ рдирд╡рдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рдкрд░рд╛рд╢рд░рд╕реНрдпрд╛рд░реНрд╖рдВ рддреНрд░реИрд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдорд╛рдЧреНрдиреЗрдпрдореН ред рдЕрдиреБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдВ рдЪ-тАЩ рд░рдпрд┐рд░реНрди ’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдкреНрд░рд╛рддрд░рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХрд╛рд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░рдпреЛрд░реБрдХреНрддреЛ рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧрдГ рее

Jamison Brereton

73
Agni
Par─Б┼Ыara ┼Ъ─Бktya
10 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
This last hymn of the Par─Б┼Ыara Agni cycle recapitulates some of the poetic devices and themes found in the earlier hymns and thus in some sense provides the close of a ring to the whole sequence. It begins with three verses dense with similes, recalling the first two hymns, I.65тАУ66, which were similarly simile rich. The three verses are entirely descriptive of Agni, particularly of the sacrificial fire in its position on the ritual ground, but the godтАЩs name is not mentioned until verse 4, where he is kindled by men.
The rest of the hymn concerns Agni as the central focus of humans, of gods, and of ritual substances (for this last, see vs. 6), Agni as a distributor and redistributor of goods and services among gods, patrons, and poets, a role summed up in the word тАЬportionтАЭ found in verses 5, 6, 7, and 10. This theme was announced in the first p─Бda of the hymn, and the тАЬwealth acquired from oneтАЩs fatherтАЭ of 1a recurs in verse 9.
Although this hymn lacks overt reference to the motifs of the Vai┼Ыv─Бnara fire and the T─Бn┼лnaptra rite, in which men and gods respectively become united by joint action involving the fire, the interrelations among men, among gods, and among men and gods depicted in this hymn recall the more explicit treat
ment of those motifs in earlier parts of the cycle. That both gods and men and, among men, both poets and patrons serve the fire in similar ways and seek similar rewards depicts these groups of beings as having a certain equality before Agni.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAgni, like patrimonial wealth, is the giver of food; he is a director, like the instrumental uctions of one learned in scripture; he rests in the sacrificial chamber like a welcome guest, and like an officiating priest, he brings prosperity on the house of the worshipper.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Who confers vitality like wealth acquired from oneтАЩs father, providing good guidance like the instruction of a perceptive man,
resting in a comfortable place like a guest whose pleasure is served, like a Hotar he has traversed the (sacrificial) seat of him who does honor.

Jamison Brereton Notes

For the complex relationship between тАШvitalityтАЩ (v├бyaс╕е) and the father, see disc. ad I.71.7. The тАЬwealth acquired from oneтАЩs fatherтАЭ also reminds us of I.70.10, where the sons divide and carry away the property of their aged father.

AgniтАЩs traversing of the (sacrificial) seat (s├бdma тАж v├н t─Бr─лt) in my opinion refers to the removal of what is later called the ─Аhavan─лya fire from the G─Бrhapatya fire at the west end of the ritual ground and its ceremonial placement at the east end.

See 2d.

Griffith

Oldenberg

He who gives vigour like wealth acquired by the fathers 1, who is a good guide like the instruction of a sage, who is pleased (by worship) like a comfortably resting guest 2, (Agni) has crossed the (sacrificial) seat of the worshipper like a Hotri.

Geldner

Der Kraft gibt wie der vom Vater ererbte Reichtum, ein guter F├╝hrer ist wie die Weisung des Kundigen, sich wohl f├╝hlt wie der behagliche ruhende Gast, er schritt den Opferplatz des Verehrers ab wie der Opferpriester.

Grassmann

Der Kraft verschafft, wie Gut, ererbt vom Vater, sch├╢n leitend ist wie Unterricht des Weisen, Und weich gebettet wie ein lieber Gastfreund, durchzog den Sitz des Frommen wie ein Priester.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe who is like the divine Sun, who know the truth (of things), preserves by his actions (his votaries) in all encounters; like nature, he is unchangeable and, like soul, is the source of happiness; he is ever to be cherished.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Amati = r┼лpa, svar┼лpa, peculiar form of nature; Like soul which is the seat and source of all happiness, so Agni, the chief agent of sacrifice is the main cause of felicity both here and hereafter: Brihad─Бraс╣Зyaka Upaniс╣гad 4.3.32

Jamison Brereton

Whose thoughts become reality like god SavitarтАЩs, who protects all communities according to his will,
lauded by many like a (royal) emblem, really present and agreeable like oneтАЩs own self, he has become desirable to install.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda a is more literally тАЬwho, like Savitar, possesses realized thoughts,тАЭ but I have adjusted the English to avoid awkwardness.

In c most tr. take saty├бс╕е as the shared term in the simile am├бtir n├б (Geldner тАЬwahr wie ein BildnisтАЭ) or as modifying am├бtiс╕е in the simile (Witzel Got┼Н тАЬwie eine verwirklichte ErscheinungтАЭ). The latter is impossible because am├бti- is feminine. The former does not convey much sense. The purport of the simile of course depends on the meaning of am├бti-, which I consider to be more concrete and specific than the usual glosses тАШappearance, form, pictureтАЩ. An am├бti- can be golden (III.38.8), broad and wide (V.62.5, VII.38.2, 45.2); it is associated with lordship (V.69.1 am├бtiс╣Г kс╣гatr├нyasya), can be displayed on a chariot box (I.64.9), and is unloosed or unfurled (V.45.2, VII.45.3). All of this suggests that it is a pennant or ensign or other flag-like object.

On the basis of its association with lordship, I suggest that it can be a royal emblem and that that is the basis for the simile here. As discussed ad I.70.9 and in Jamison forthcoming, pr├б тИЪ┼Ыaс╣Гs тАШproclaim, laudтАЩ is a lexeme particularly appropriate to kings, and here Agni is lauded by many like the royal emblem, which is the symbol of the king. This interpretation leaves p─Бda-final saty├бс╕е somewhat stranded, and I read it with the following p─Бda. Perhaps it was stationed in the c p─Бda because of saty├б(manm─Б) in almost the same position in the a p─Бda. Alternatively it can simply be another qualifier of Agni in b, independent of the simile: тАЬlauded by many like a (royal) emblem, real тАжтАЭ Most tr. give a rather vague and general rendering of the morphologically elaborate desiderative gerundive didhiс╣г─Б╠Бyyaс╕е, тАЬdesirable to hold/winтАЩ. I think it has a more technical ritual sense, referring to the installation of the fire (so also in the other occurrence of this form in II.4.1). This would reflect the same sense of тИЪdh─Б as the adjective pur├│hita-, of the fire тАШplaced/installed in front/to the eastтАЩ and the later ritual complex the Agny─Бdheya тАШestablishment of the fire(s)тАЩ. If my interpr. of 1d is correct, namely that the offering fire has been taken from west to east, then the next step would be its installation in the east.

Griffith

He who like Savitar the God, true-minded protecteth with his power. all acts of vigour,
Truthful, like splendour, glorified by many, like breath joy-giving,–all must strive to win him.

Oldenberg

He who being truthful like the god Savitri 1 protects by his power of mind all settlements 2, praised by many like impetuous splendour 3, the truthful one has become dear like vital breath and worthy to be searched for 4.

Geldner

Der aufrichtig in seinem Sinn wie der Gott Savitri, mit Umsicht alle Opferparteien ├╝berwacht, von vielen gepriesen, wahr wie ein Bildnis, lieb wie das eigene Selbst - ihn soll man zu halten suchen.

Grassmann

Der treugesinnt wie Savitar, der Gott, ist, und alle St├дtten schirmt mit seiner Weisheit, Der vielger├╝hmte, lauter wie der Lichtglanz, ist w├╝nschenswerth wie holder Lebensodem.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe who, like the divine (Sun), is the supporter of the universe, abides on earth like a prince, (surrounded by) faithful friends; in his presence, men sit down like sons in the dwelling of a parent, and (in purity he resembles) an irreproachable and beloved wife.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Who, suckling all, dwells peacefully upon the earth, like a god, like a king with established alliances,
stationed in front like heroes stationed for protection, irreproachable like a wife pleasing to her husbandтАФ

Jamison Brereton Notes

For the first three p─Бdas, cf. III.55.21.

The construction of this verse is more complex than the two preceding ones and, in my opinion, displays some tricky relationships with Par─Б┼ЫaraтАЩs phraseology elsewhere. To begin with, the first simile as it stands is pleonastic+++(=redundant)+++ at best: Agni should not be тАЬlike a god,тАЭ since he is a god. Nor should he be тАЬlike a god who dwells on earth,тАЭ since in fact Agni is the only god, or (counting Soma) the primary god, who dwells on earth. I suggest tentatively that the opening dev├│ n├б is there to match n├б r─Б╠Бj─Б at the end of the hemistich. Even more tentatively I suggest that what is really being compared is pс╣Ыthiv─л╠Бс╣Г vi┼Ыv├бdh─Бy─Б(с╕е). Note first that in the preceding hymn (10cd) mother earth spread out тАЬto suckle the bird [probably =Agni]тАЭ (dh─Б╠Бyase v├йс╕е) and elsewhere earth is called тАЬall-nourishingтАЭ (II.17.5 pс╣Ыthiv─л╠Бс╣Г vi┼Ыv├бdh─Бyasam).

I think here that Par─Б┼Ыara is covertly comparing Agni to the earth with regard to this well-known trait of hers, but does so playfully and allusively by stationing acc. pс╣Ыthiv─л╠Бm next to nom. vi┼Ыv├бdh─Бy─Б(с╕е) (in the same metrical position as II.17.5 though in Triс╣гс╣нubh not Jagat─л cadence) and by the intertextual associations evoked by his stating that earth suckled Agni in I.72.9. So the, or an, underlying meaning of p─Бda a is тАЬthe god who, all-nourishing like the earth, тАж,тАЭ though both the position of the simile marker and the case of тАШearthтАЩ disallow this as a surface meaning. (Let me make clear that I am not suggesting emending the text to *pс╣Ыthiv─л╠Б.) The two compounds hit├б(mitra-) (b) and puraс╕е(s├бdaс╕е) may make implicit reference to the word I suggested is to be associated with didhiс╣г─Б╠Бyyaс╕е in 2d, namely pur├│-hita, as a descriptor of the installed ritual fire. The second, puraс╕еs├бd-, is essentially a synonym of pur├│hita-.

Although I try to avoid explanations like тАЬattraction,тАЭ I am afraid I must follow Geldner in taking the common term of the similes in c and d as тАЬattractedтАЭ to the comparandum: pur├бс╕еsadaс╕е to the pl. v─лr─Б╠Бс╕е from putative sg. *pur├бс╕еsad, anavady─Б╠Бto the fem. n─Б╠Бr─л from putative masc. *anavady├бс╕е. Although it would be possible to avoid the attraction analysis by reading both terms as part of the simile proper (тАЬlike heroes stationed in front and stationed for protection, like an irreproachable wife pleasing to her husband,тАЭ so Witzel Got┼Н), this puts the simile marker one element too far to the right and it also submerges the common term. This would be particularly unfortunate in the first simile, since there is a play on two slightly different senses of

-s├бd- there. (In I.65.5 a similar gender mismatch is found, explained by Renou as attraction, an explanation I rejected. But there it does not involve a misplaced simile marker.)

Griffith

He who on earth dwells like a king surrounded by faithful friends, like a God all-sustaining,
Like heroes who preside, who sit in safety: like as a blameless dame dear to her husband.

(Agni) who possessing every refreshment dwells on the earth like a god, like a king who has made himself (valiant) friends 2, like heroes who sit in front and under shelter, like a blameless wife beloved by her husband.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSuch as you are, Agni, men preserve you constantly kindled in their dwellings, in secure plural ces, and offer upon you abundant (sacrificial) food; do you, in whom is all existence, be the bearer of riches (for our advantage).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You, o Agni, kindled here in the house as their own, do men attend on in their fixed abodes.
They deposited abundant heavenly brilliance within him. Become the foundation of riches for your whole lifetime!

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted at I.72.10 our c is almost identical to p─Бda a there. The published translation

treats the first as a T─Бnun─Бptra passage (тАЬdeposited their own ┼Ыr─л╠БтАЭ) but not this one, and the two should probably be brought into harmony. I now favor taking neither one as a T─Бnun─Бptra expression, but see disc. ad I.72.10. In this case the deposit of тАШheavenly brillianceтАЩ (dyumn├б-) may be what allows Agni to become the foundation of riches.

Griffith

Thee, such, in settlements secure, O Agni, our men serve ever kindled in each dwelling.
On him have they laid splendour in abundance: dear to all men, bearer be he of riches.

Oldenberg

Thee, O Agni, who art constantly kindled in the house, men have worshipped in their firm dwellings. They have placed in him rich splendour 1. Be thou possessed of all life, a supporter of riches 2.

Geldner

Dir, Agni, der best├дndig im Hause entz├╝ndet wird, leisten die M├дnner in den festen Wohnsitzen Folge. Viel Ehre haben sie auf ihn geh├дuft. Sei du lebensl├дnglich der Tr├дger von Reicht├╝mern!

Grassmann

So, Agni, sind um dich, den stets entflammten, im Haus die M├дnner in den festen Sitzen, Viel sch├╢nes haben sie in dich gesenket, sei allbelebend unsers Reichthums Tr├дger.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay your opulent worshippers, Agni, obtain (abundant) food; may the learned (who praise you) and offer you (oblations), acquire long life; may we gain in battles booty from our foes, presenting their portion to the gods for (the acquisition of) renown.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Might the bounteous ones reach nourishments, o Agni, and (might) the patrons who give (reach) through a whole lifetime.
Might we gain the victory-prize in our clashes with the stranger,
acquiring a portion among the gods for our fame.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The verb v├н тАж a┼Ыyuс╕е should be read with both p─Бdas, but, in my opinion, with slightly different senses. In p─Бda a pс╣Ы╠Бkс╣гaс╕е is a straight acc. object to the lexeme in the meaning тАШreach, attainтАЩ; in p─Бda b v├н┼Ыvam ─Б╠Бyuс╕е may be one too (тАЬattain a whole lifetimeтАЭ) as most take it, but it may also be an acc. of extent of time (тАЬreach through a whole lifetimeтАЭ). The meaning is almost the same, but it would be like Par─Б┼Ыara to put the constructions slightly off-balance, and the compound vi┼Ыv─Б╠Бyuс╕е is something of a signature word for Par─Б┼Ыara (see the immediately preceding vs. 4d, plus I.67.6, 10, 68.5) as an adverb expressing extent of time (тАЬlifelong,тАЭ etc.). Note the phonetic echoes, p─Бda a: v├н тАж a┼Ыyur, b: v├н тАж ─Б╠Бyuс╕е; the first of these distracted sequences also evokes vi┼Ыv─Б╠Бyuс╕е.

P─Бda c san├йma тАж ary├│ is reminiscent of I.70.1a van├йma тАж ary├│ тАж The phrase bh─Бg├бс╣Г dev├йс╣гu тАж d├бdh─Бn─Бс╕е is almost a paraphrase of I.68.4a bh├бjanta тАж devatv├бm. I would therefore change the published translation тАЬa portion among the godsтАЭ to тАЬa share in the gods.тАЭ

Griffith

May thy rich worshippers win food, O Agni, and princes gain long life who bring oblation.
May we get booty from our foe in battle, presenting to the Gods their share for glory.

Oldenberg

May the liberal givers, O Agni, attain nourishment, may the rich 1 who bestow gifts (on us) attain to a full span of life. May we win in battles the booty of him who does not give 1, obtaining a (rich) share before the gods, that we may win glory 2.

Geldner

Unsere G├╢nner sollen Lebenskr├дfte erlangen, o Agni, die schenkenden Herren das volle Leben. Wir wollen den Siegerpreis gewinnen in den Wettk├дmpfen mit dem Nebenbuhler, von den G├╢ttern unser Teil empfangend zum Ruhme.

Grassmann

Die reichen F├╝rsten, Agni, welche spenden, lass Speis’ erlangen, volle Lebensdauer, Uns treue lass in K├дmpfen Gut erbeuten, die wir zum Ruhm ihr Theil den G├╢ttern geben.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe cows, loving (Agni, who has come to thehall of sacrifice), sharing his splendour, have brought with full udders (their milk) to be drunk. The rivers, soliciting his good will, have flowed from a distance in the vicinity of the mountain.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For the bellowing cows of truth, apportioned by heaven, swell with their udders;
from afar, seeking a portion of (your?) favor, the rivers have flowed
forth all at once over the rock.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The referents of the тАЬcows of truthтАЭ (ab) and the rivers (cd) are unclear, nor is it clear whether they refer to the same thing. But I think they must be evaluated in the context of this hymn, in which men (vs. 4), patrons (vs. 5), and gods (vs. 7) all serve Agni in one way or another and seek rewards from him; the cows and the rivers then must be another set of devotees and aspirants to his favor, esp. since the same phrase sumat├нm bh├нkс╣гam─Бс╣З─Б(с╕е) тАЬseeking a portion of favorтАЭ is used of the rivers (6c) and the worship-worthy (gods) (7a). I would tentatively suggest a twofold interpretation: 1) A naturalistic one: the swelling cows are the rains, тАЬapportioned by heaven,тАЭ with their bellowing the thunder and the udders the clouds. The rains both are the (heavenly) rivers and feed the (earthly) rivers. Recall the seven heavenly rivers of

Griffith

The cows of holy law, sent us by Heaven, have swelled with laden udders, loudly lowing;
Soliciting his favour, from a distance the rivers to the rock have flowed together.

Oldenberg

The lowing milch-cows of Rita, assigned by Heaven, were exuberant with their full udders. The rivers imploring the favour (of the gods) from afar have broken through the midst of the rock with their floods.

Denn die K├╝he, die sich nach der Ordnung richten, strotzen br├╝llend mit gleichvollen Eutern, die von den Himmlischen geschenkten. Von weitem sind die Fl├╝sse mitten durch den Fels hervorgebrochen, indem sie sich die Gunst ausbitten.

Laut br├╝llend schwollen an des Opfers K├╝he mit vollem Euter, sie, des Himmels Gabe; Von Ferne her nach Huld verlangend flossen quer durch den festen Fels hindurch die Str├╢me.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(The gods), who are entitled to worship, soliciting your good will, have entrusted to you, resplendent Agni, the (sacrificial) food, and, (for the due observance of sacred rites), they have made the night and morning of different colours, or black and purple.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Seeking a portion of favor in you, those worthy of worship [=gods] set their fame in heaven.
They made night and dawn of different forms, and they put together the black color and the red.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The voc. agne was inadvertently omitted from the published translation, so тАЬo AgniтАЭ should be inserted after тАЬin you.тАЭ The second p─Бda could also mean тАЬthey acquired fame in heaven.тАЭ The phrase should be read with 5d bh─Бg├бс╣Г dev├йс╣гu ┼Ыr├бvase d├бdh─Бn─Бс╕е and 10c ├бdhi ┼Ыr├бvo dev├бbhaktaс╣Г d├бdh─Бn─Бс╕е. The latter passage, especially, suggests that тАШacquireтАЩ is the better rendering.

The accented cakr├║с╕е in c can be explained, following Klein (DGRV I.176-77), as triggered by the тАЬrhetorically complementary nature of p─Бdas c and d.тАЭ There is no need to take the ca in c as a subordinator, particularly because subordinating ca introduces conditional clauses. Note the contrast between v├н(r┼лpe) and s├бс╣Г (dhuс╕е), a common rhetorical pairing.

Griffith

Agni, with thee, soliciting thy favour, the holy Ones have gained glory in heaven.
They made the Night and Dawn of different colours, and set the black and purple hues together.

Oldenberg

Imploring favour from thee, O Agni, the worshipful (gods) have won glory in the sky. They have made Night and Dawn of different shapes; they have joined the black and red colour (to Night and Dawn).

Geldner

Indem sie von dir, Agni, sich die Gunst ausbitten, haben die Opferw├╝rdigen im Himmel Ruhm erworben. Sie haben Nacht und Morgen, die ungleichen, geschaffen, die dunkle und die r├╢tliche Farbe aneinander gef├╝gt.

Grassmann

Von dir, o Agni, holden Sinn erbittend, erlangten Ruhm im Himmel die verehrten; Sie machten ungleichfarbig Nacht und Morgen, die rothe Farbe an die schwarze f├╝gend.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay we, mortals, whom you have directed (to the performance of sacrifices) for the sake of riches, become opulent; filling heaven and earth, and the firmament (with your radiance), you protect the whole world like a (sheltering) shade.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Might weтАФwe and our patronsтАФbe those mortals whom you will sweeten for wealth, o Agni.
Like a shadow you accompany all creation, having filled the two
world-halves and the space between.

Griffith

May we and those who worship be the mortals whom thou, O Agni, leadest on to riches.
Thou hast filled earth and heaven and air’s mid-region, and followest the whole world like a shadow.

Oldenberg

And may we, our liberal givers and ourselves, be the mortals whom thou furtherest to wealth, O Agni 1. Like a shadow thou followest the whole world, having filled the two worlds (Heaven and Earth) and the air 2.

Geldner

Unsere G├╢nner und wir m├╢chten die Sterblichen sein, die du zum Reichtum w├╝rdig machst, o Agni. Wie der Schatten begleitest du die ganze Welt, nachdem du Himmel und Erde, den Luftraum erf├╝llt hast.

Grassmann

Wir und die F├╝rsten seien unter denen, die du zu reichem Gute f├╝hrst, o Agni, Gleich wie der Schatten folgst du jedem Wesen die Luft, den Himmel und die Erd’ erf├╝llend.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рдЬрдЧрджреАрд╢реНрд╡рд░ ! рдпрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рдпрд╛рдиреН рд╕реБрд╕реВрджреЛ рдорд░реНрддреНрддрд╛рдирд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рд░рд╛рдпреЗ рд╕рд┐рд╕рдХреНрд╖рд┐, рддреЗ рд╡рдпрдВ рдордШрд╡рд╛рдирдГ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдоред рдпреЛ рднрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЫрд╛рдпреЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рдВ рднреБрд╡рдирдВ рд░реЛрджрд╕реА рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдВ рдЪрд╛рдкрдкреНрд░рд┐рд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрддрд╡рд╛рдирд╕рд┐ рддрдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗ рд╡рдпрдореБрдкрд╛рд╕реНрдорд╣реЗ рее рео рее

рдЕрдереИрддрддреНрд╕реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдХрд░реНрддреНрддреЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рдГ рдХреАрджреГрд╢реЛрд╜рд╕реНрддреАрддреНрдпреБрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрддреЗ рее

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдпрд╛рдиреН) рдЙрддреНрддрдорд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рдиреН (рд░рд╛рдпреЗ) рдзрдирд╛рдп (рдорд░реНрддреНрддрд╛рдиреН) рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреН (рд╕реБрд╕реВрджрдГ) рдХреНрд╖рдпрд╢рд░реАрд░рд╛рджрд┐рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдиреН (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ) рдЬрдЧрджреАрд╢реНрд╡рд░ (рддреЗ) рддрд╡ (рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо) рднрд╡реЗрдо (рдордШрд╡рд╛рдирдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрддрдзрдирдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдГ (рд╡рдпрдореН) рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рдирдГ (рдЪ) рд╕рдореБрдЪреНрдЪрдпреЗ (рдЫрд╛рдпреЗрд╡) рдпрдерд╛ рд╢рд░реАрд░реИрдГ рд╕рд╣ рдЫрд╛рдпрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрддреЗ рддрдерд╛ (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рдореН) рдЕрдЦрд┐рд▓рдореН (рднреБрд╡рдирдореН) рдЬрдЧрддреН (рд╕рд┐рд╕рдХреНрд╖рд┐) рд╕рдорд╡реИрддрд┐ (рдЖрдкрдкреНрд░рд┐рд╡рд╛рдиреН) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреЛ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрддрд╡рд╛рдиреН (рд░реЛрджрд╕реА) рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпреМ (рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдореН) рдЖрдХрд╛рд╢рдореН рее рео рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDefended, Agni, by you, may we destroy the horses (of your enemies) by (our) horses, their men by (our) men, their sons by (our) sons, and may our sons, learned and inheritors of ancestral wealth, live for a hundred winters.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Might we vanquish steeds with steeds, men with men, and heroes with heroes, o Agni, when aided by you.
As lords of wealth acquired from their fathers, might our patrons,
having a hundred winters, reach through (a whole lifetime).

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the echo of I.70.1, with optatives to the same (synchronic) root and a likely identical case frame. See disc. ad I.70.1.

The second hemistich reprises material from earlier in the hymn: тАЬwealth acquired from their fathersтАЭ is exactly the same phrase, though in a different case, as the simile that begins the hymn (I.73.1a); the patrons with their long lives were encountered in 5b.

Griffith

Aided by thee, O Agni, may we conquer steeds with steeds, men with men, heroes with heroes,
Lords of the wealth transmitted by our fathers: and may our princes live a hundred winters.

Oldenberg

May we, O Agni, guarded by thee, conquer with our racers the racers, with our men the men, with our heroes the heroes (of our enemies). Being masters of the riches which their fathers 1 have conquered, may our rich (givers) reach a hundred winters.

Geldner

Mit den Rennpferden wollen wir, o Agni, die Rennpferde, mit den Mannen die Mannen, mit S├╢hnen die S├╢hne ├╝berbieten durch deinen Beistand. Im Besitz des vom Vater geerbten Reichtums sollen unsere Herren auf hundert Winter ihr Leben bringen.

Grassmann

Mit dir lass Renner uns durch Renner schlagen, durch M├дnner M├дnner und durch Helden Helden, Lass unsre F├╝rsten hundert Jahr’ erreichen, verf├╝gend ├╝ber den ererbten Reichthum.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay these our praises, sapient Agni, be grateful to you, both in mind and heart; may we be competent to detain your well-supporting wealth, offering upon you their share of the (sacrificial food of the gods).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let these solemn speeches be pleasing to you, o Agni, ritual expertтАФto your mind and heart.
Might we be able to control (the prizewinning horses) of your wealth, (so they are) amenable to the chariot-pole, while we acquire the fame apportioned by the gods.
The next, rather sizable group of twenty hymns is attributed to Gotama R─Бh┼лgaс╣Зa, who could be the father or other ancestor of the poet of I.58тАУ64, Nodhas Gautama. If so, the dazzling skill of the son is not on view in the work of his father in the opening Agni hymns (74тАУ79) or in the All God hymns (89тАУ90), which seem more dutiful than engaged, but when he treats other gods, especially the Maruts (85тАУ88) and Dawn (92), his poetry can be inspired.

Jamison Brereton Notes

GeldnerтАЩs interpr. of p─Бda c is persuasive. II.5.1 ┼Ыak├йma v─Бj├нno y├бmam (also III.27.3, VIII.24.22) contains the missing horses supplied here. I take sudh├║raс╕е as proleptic.

For p─Бda d cf. 5d and 7b; for dev├бbhakta- cf. dy├║bhakta- in 6b.

Griffith

May these our hymns of praise, Agni, Ordainer, be pleasant to thee in thy heart and spirit.
May we have power to hold thy steeds of riches, laying on thee the God-sent gift of glory.

Oldenberg

May these hymns, O Agni, worshipper (of the gods), be grateful to thee, to thy mind and heart. May we be able to bridle thee, the well-harnessed wealth 1, acquiring the glory which the gods have assigned us.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ (рд╡реЗрдзрдГ) рд╕рдмрдХреЗ рдЕрдиреНрддрдГрдХрд░рдг рдореЗрдВ рд░рд╣рдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рд╕рдмрдХреЛ рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐рдкреНрд░рдж рдзрд░реНрддреНрддрд╛ (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ) рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рдХреЗ рджреЗрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдЬрдЧрджреАрд╢реНрд╡рд░ (рддреЗ) рдЖрдкрдХреА рдХреГрдкрд╛ рд╕реЗ (рдПрддрд╛) (рдЙрдЪрдерд╛рдирд┐) рд╡реЗрджрд╡рдЪрди рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЗ (рдордирд╕реЗ) рдорди (рдЪ) рдФрд░ (рд╣реГрджреЗ) рдЖрддреНрдорд╛ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рдЬреБрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдирд┐) рд╕реЗрд╡рди рдХрд┐рдпреЗ рд╣реБрдП рдкреНрд░реАрддрд┐рдХрд╛рд░рдХ (рд╕рдиреНрддреБ) рд╣реЛрд╡реЗрдВ, рд╡реЗ (рддреЗ) рдЖрдкрдХреЗ рд╕рдореНрдмрдиреНрдз рд╕реЗ (рдпрдордореН) рдирд┐рдпрдо рдХрд░рдиреЗ (рджреЗрд╡рднрдХреНрддрдореН) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдиреЗ рд╕реЗрд╡рди рдХрд┐рдпреЗ рд╣реБрдП (рд╢реНрд░рд╡рдГ) рд╢реНрд░рд╡рдг рдХреЛ (рджрдзрд╛рдирд╛рдГ) рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реБрдП (рд╕реБрдзреБрд░рдГ) рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдереЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧ (рд░рд╛рдпрдГ) рдзрдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рдХреЛ (рдЕрдзрд┐ рд╢рдХреЗрдо) рд╕рдорд░реНрде рд╣реЛрдВ рее резреж рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рдХрд┐ рдЖрдк рд╕рдм рд╕реБрдЦреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрдХрд░ рдФрд░ рд╕рднреА рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░рд╛рд╡реЗрдВ рее резреж рее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░, рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐, рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдФрд░ рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрде рдХреА рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рд╕рдордЭрдиреА рдЙрдЪрд┐рдд рд╣реИ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рд╡реЗрдзреЛрд╜рдЧреНрдиреЗ рдЬрдЧрджреАрд╢реНрд╡рд░ ! рддреЗ рддрд╡ рдХреГрдкрдпреИрддреЛрдЪрдерд╛рдиреНрдпрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рдордирд╕реЗ рд╣реГрджреЗ рдЪ рдЬреБрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдирд┐ рд╕рдиреНрддреБ рддреЗ рддрд╡ рд╕рдореНрдмрдиреНрдзреЗрди рдпрдордВ рджреЗрд╡рднрдХреНрддрдВ рд╢реНрд░рд╡реЛ рджрдзрд╛рдирд╛рдГ рд╕реБрдзреБрд░реЛ рд╡рдпрдВ рд░рд╛рдпрд╛ рдзрдирд╛рдирд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддреБрдордзрд┐ рд╢рдХреЗрдо рее резреж рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдВ рддрддреНрд╕рд╣рд╛рдпреЗрди рдХрд┐рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдпрдд рдЗрддреНрдпреБрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрддреЗ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдПрддрд╛) рдПрддрд╛рдирд┐ (рддреЗ) рддрд╡ (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ) рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдкреНрд░рдж (рдЙрдЪрдерд╛рдирд┐) рд╡реЗрджрд╡рдЪрдирд╛рдирд┐ (рд╡реЗрдзрдГ) рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдкреНрд░рдж (рдЬреБрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдирд┐) рдкреНрд░реАрддрд╛рдирд┐ рд╕реЗрд╡рд┐рддрд╛рдирд┐ (рд╕рдиреНрддреБ) рднрд╡рдиреНрддреБ (рдордирд╕реЗ) (рд╣реГрджреЗ) рдЖрддреНрдордиреЗ (рдЪ) рд╕рдореБрдЪреНрдЪрдпреЗ (рд╢рдХреЗрдо) рд╢рдХреНрдиреБрдпрд╛рдоред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпреЗрди рд╢рдкреНред (рд░рд╛рдпрдГ) рдзрдирд╛рдирд┐ (рд╕реБрдзреБрд░рдГ) рд╢реЛрднрдирд╛ рдзреБрд░реЛ рдзрд╛рд░рдгрд╛рдирд┐ рдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдиреНрддреЗ (рдпрдордореН) рдпрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ рдпреЗрди рддрдореН (рддреЗ) рддрд╡ (рдЕрдзрд┐) рдЙрдкрд░рд┐рднрд╛рд╡реЗ (рд╢реНрд░рд╡рдГ) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╢реНрд░рд╡рдгрдореН (рджреЗрд╡рднрдХреНрддрдореН) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрднрд┐рдГ рд╕реЗрд╡рд┐рддрдореН (рджрдзрд╛рдирд╛рдГ) рдзрд░рдиреНрддрдГ рее резреж рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреИрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдгрд┐ рд╕реБрдЦрд╛рдирд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдп рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрднреНрдпрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдпрд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдирд┐ рее резреж рее рдЕрддреНрд░реЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рддреНрд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдпрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░рд╕реНрддреАрддрд┐ рд╡реЗрджрд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрдореН рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ
